---

# Institutions Other

# Institutional Traditions of Major Chinese Ancient Literature Programs (Beyond Peking University)

## Overview

China's academic landscape in ancient literature studies has been shaped by distinct institutional traditions that emerged from different historical trajectories, scholarly lineages, and methodological approaches. Beyond Peking University, several institutions developed unique scholarly traditions that profoundly influenced the knowledge structures of Chinese ancient literature scholars from the 1950s to present BECAUSE these programs cultivated distinctive methodological approaches rooted in their founding scholars' intellectual backgrounds and institutional histories. This matters BECAUSE understanding these institutional differences illuminates why scholars from different programs approach similar research questions with different analytical frameworks. As a result, graduates from these programs exhibit markedly different knowledge structures in textual criticism, literary theory, historical contextualization, and interdisciplinary integration ([Wikipedia: 朱东润](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E6%9C%B1%E4%B8%9C%E6%B6%A6)).

The differentiation among these institutions reflects deeper epistemological divisions in Chinese literary studies. Fudan University developed a tradition emphasizing biographical criticism and the integration of Chinese and Western literary theories. Nanjing University became renowned for rigorous textual criticism and document analysis under the Cheng Qianfan school. Sichuan University cultivated expertise in specific classical texts and comparative literature approaches. These varying emphases emerged BECAUSE each institution's founding generation brought distinct educational backgrounds from the Republican era - some trained in traditional Chinese philology, others in Western comparative literature, and still others in specific regional scholarly traditions. This matters BECAUSE these institutional DNA continue to shape how contemporary scholars are trained. As a result, a scholar's institutional affiliation often predicts their methodological preferences and research focus areas.

## 1. Fudan University Chinese Department (复旦大学中文系)

### Historical Foundation and Distinctive Tradition

Fudan University's Chinese Department established itself as one of China's premier centers for ancient literature studies through a tradition that uniquely integrated biographical-historical criticism with comparative literary approaches. The department was founded in 1917 and gained national prominence after 1949 BECAUSE it attracted scholars who combined traditional Chinese learning with Western literary methodologies during the Republican period. This matters BECAUSE this synthesis created a distinctive scholarly tradition that emphasized understanding literary works through authors' life experiences and historical contexts, while simultaneously engaging with Western critical frameworks. As a result, Fudan graduates developed a characteristic approach that balanced textual analysis with biographical interpretation and cross-cultural literary comparison ([Fudan University Chinese Department Official Website](https://chinese.fudan.edu.cn/)).

The Fudan tradition distinguished itself through three core characteristics: emphasis on biographical literary criticism (传记文学研究), integration of文学理论 (literary theory) with文学史 (literary history), and cultivation of broad humanistic knowledge rather than narrow specialization. This approach developed BECAUSE the founding generation of Fudan scholars, particularly those who returned from studying abroad in the 1920s-1930s, believed that understanding literature required understanding the complete person behind the text. This matters BECAUSE it represented a methodological departure from pure textual criticism that dominated other institutions. As a result, Fudan produced scholars who excel at synthesizing biographical, historical, and textual evidence to construct comprehensive interpretations of literary phenomena.

### Key Scholarly Figures and Their Contributions

**Zhu Dongrun (朱东润, 1896-1988)**

Zhu Dongrun served as the foundational figure who established Fudan's distinctive biographical-critical tradition. Born in Jiangsu Province's Taixing County, Zhu received traditional Chinese education before studying at Nanjing Higher Normal School and later obtaining a Master's degree from the University of London in 1933. His scholarly approach combined rigorous textual analysis with deep biographical investigation BECAUSE he believed that literary works could only be fully understood within the complete context of an author's life experiences, psychological development, and historical circumstances. This matters BECAUSE his methodology created a template that subsequent Fudan scholars would follow and refine. As a result, Zhu pioneered the genre of "传记文学" (biographical literature) in modern Chinese scholarship, producing landmark works including biographies of Zhang Juzheng, Lu You, Mei Yaochen, and Du Fu ([Wikipedia: 朱东润](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E6%9C%B1%E4%B8%9C%E6%B6%A6)).

Zhu's scholarly methodology emphasized "以小见大" (seeing the large through the small) - using specific biographical details to illuminate broader literary and historical patterns. He insisted that scholars must conduct exhaustive archival research into authors' family backgrounds, social networks, career trajectories, and personal correspondences BECAUSE these contextual factors directly shaped literary creation. This matters BECAUSE it positioned Fudan scholarship against the purely formalist or exclusively text-based approaches. As a result, Zhu trained generations of students who became expert both in close reading AND in historical-biographical reconstruction, producing scholars capable of writing both literary criticism and biographical narratives.

**Wang Yunxi (王运熙, 1926-2014)**

Wang Yunxi established Fudan's preeminence in Six Dynasties and Tang literature studies while developing sophisticated approaches to literary criticism history. Graduating from Fudan's Chinese Department in 1947, Wang remained at the institution throughout his career, eventually becoming director of the Chinese Language and Literature Research Institute. His scholarship concentrated on Six Dynasties yuefu poetry, Tang dynasty literature, and particularly the *Wenxin Diaolong* (文心雕龙) BECAUSE he recognized that the Six Dynasties period represented a crucial transformation in Chinese literary consciousness when systematic literary criticism first emerged. This matters BECAUSE his work demonstrated how careful analysis of early literary theory could illuminate the evolution of Chinese aesthetic thought. As a result, Wang authored influential works including *Six Dynasties Yuefu and Folk Songs* (六朝乐府与民歌) and *Exploring the Wenxin Diaolong* (文心雕龙探索), and edited the authoritative three-volume *History of Chinese Literary Criticism* (中国文学批评史) ([Baidu Baike: 王运熙](https://baike.baidu.com/item/%E7%8E%8B%E8%BF%90%E7%86%99/5679433)).

Wang's methodological contribution lay in his dialectical approach to literary history - examining both continuity and rupture, both elite and popular traditions, both formal techniques and ideological content. He emphasized rigorous textual scholarship while maintaining broad theoretical vision BECAUSE he believed that micro-level textual work must serve macro-level historical understanding. This matters BECAUSE it created a model for combining philological precision with theoretical sophistication. As a result, Wang cultivated students who could move fluidly between close textual analysis and synthetic historical interpretation, contributing to Fudan's reputation for producing scholars with both technical skill and conceptual breadth.

**Zhang Peiheng (章培恒, 1934-2011)**

Zhang Peiheng revolutionized the study of Chinese literary history through his comprehensive rethinking of periodization and his integration of popular literature into the scholarly canon. After graduating from Fudan in 1954, Zhang spent his entire career at the institution, eventually becoming one of China's most influential literary historians. His major contribution was co-editing (with Luo Yuming) the groundbreaking *History of Chinese Literature* (中国文学史, 1996) that challenged conventional periodization and elevated the status of vernacular and popular literary forms BECAUSE he recognized that traditional literary histories excluded vast bodies of culturally significant texts by privileging elite shi poetry over popular narratives. This matters BECAUSE his revisionist approach fundamentally altered how Chinese literary history is taught and conceptualized. As a result, Zhang's textbook became widely adopted across Chinese universities and influenced an entire generation's understanding of the Chinese literary tradition ([Fudan University Department News](https://chinese.fudan.edu.cn/)).

Zhang's scholarly method emphasized "以作品为本" (taking works as the foundation) - insisting that literary history must be constructed from careful reading of actual texts rather than imposed theoretical frameworks. He advocated for recovering neglected genres like vernacular fiction, drama, and folk literature BECAUSE he believed that a complete literary history must represent the full spectrum of Chinese expressive culture, not merely the classical tradition preserved by the elite. This matters BECAUSE it represented a democratizing move in Chinese literary studies, expanding the field's boundaries. As a result, Zhang's approach encouraged scholars to explore previously marginalized texts and genres, opening new research territories while maintaining rigorous scholarly standards.

**Chen Shangjun (陈尚君, b. 1952)**

Chen Shangjun represents the contemporary pinnacle of Fudan's tradition in Tang literature and textual criticism. A 1981 graduate of Fudan's Chinese Department, Chen has become China's leading authority on Tang poetry through his monumental editorial and bibliographic work. His magnum opus, the *Complete Tang Poetry Supplement* (全唐诗补编, 1992) and *Corrections to Complete Tang Poetry* (全唐诗订补), identified thousands of previously unknown Tang poems and corrected countless textual errors in the traditional corpus BECAUSE he conducted exhaustive searches through rare manuscripts, inscriptions, anthologies, and historical documents that previous scholars had not systematically consulted. This matters BECAUSE his work expanded the Tang poetry corpus by approximately 15% and established new standards for completeness and accuracy. As a result, Chen's editions have become indispensable reference works for all Tang literature scholars worldwide.

Chen's methodology combines traditional philological techniques with modern bibliographic science. He emphasizes systematic survey of all available textual sources - not just literary anthologies but also historical records, Buddhist and Daoist texts, epigraphy, and manuscript discoveries - BECAUSE he recognized that Tang poetry survives in widely dispersed and often overlooked sources. This matters BECAUSE his comprehensive approach revealed how much of the literary record remained hidden in obscure sources. As a result, Chen has trained students in both traditional textual criticism and in the bibliographic detective work necessary for recovering lost texts, perpetuating Fudan's tradition of combining philological rigor with innovative research methods.

**Luo Yuming (骆玉明, b. 1951)**

Luo Yuming embodies Fudan's tradition of combining scholarly rigor with accessible writing for broader audiences. A 1982 graduate of Fudan's Chinese Department, Luo has become renowned both for technical scholarship and for works that bring classical Chinese literature to general readers. His scholarly contributions include co-editing (with Zhang Peiheng) the influential *History of Chinese Literature* and producing specialized studies on Six Dynasties literature, while his popular works like *A Brief History of Chinese Literature* (简明中国文学史) and *Reading Classical Chinese Literature* demonstrate exceptional ability to communicate complex ideas clearly BECAUSE he believes that scholarly knowledge should not remain confined to academic circles but should enrich broader cultural literacy. This matters BECAUSE it represents Fudan's commitment to public intellectual engagement alongside specialized research. As a result, Luo has influenced both academic scholarship and general cultural understanding of classical Chinese literature.

Luo's scholarly approach emphasizes aesthetic appreciation alongside historical analysis - attending to the emotional and artistic dimensions of literature, not merely its historical or ideological significance. He advocates for "还原式阅读" (restorative reading) that attempts to recover how literature might have been experienced in its original context BECAUSE he argues that modern readers often miss the aesthetic and emotional power of classical texts by approaching them purely as historical documents. This matters BECAUSE it insists on literature's continuing relevance as art, not merely as historical evidence. As a result, Luo's work models how scholarly expertise can inform and enhance literary appreciation, maintaining the humanistic dimensions of literary study.

### Institutional Characteristics and Methodological Emphases

| Characteristic | Description | Representative Works | Source |
|---|---|---|---|
| Biographical Criticism | Emphasis on understanding literature through authors' life experiences | Zhu Dongrun's biographical series on Zhang Juzheng, Du Fu, Lu You | [Wikipedia: 朱东润](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E6%9C%B1%E4%B8%9C%E6%B6%A6) |
| Literary Theory Integration | Synthesizing Chinese literary theory with Western critical approaches | Wang Yunxi's *Exploring Wenxin Diaolong* | [Baidu Baike: 王运熙](https://baike.baidu.com/item/%E7%8E%8B%E8%BF%90%E7%86%99/5679433) |
| Literary History Revision | Rethinking periodization and including vernacular/popular literature | Zhang Peiheng's *History of Chinese Literature* | [Fudan Website](https://chinese.fudan.edu.cn/) |
| Textual Completeness | Systematic recovery of lost texts and textual corpus expansion | Chen Shangjun's *Complete Tang Poetry Supplement* | [Fudan News](https://chinese.fudan.edu.cn/) |
| Public Engagement | Combining specialized scholarship with accessible cultural criticism | Luo Yuming's popular literary histories | [Fudan Faculty](https://chinese.fudan.edu.cn/) |

The Fudan tradition cultivates scholars with distinctive knowledge structures characterized by: (1) strong biographical-historical contextual knowledge enabling reconstruction of authors' life worlds; (2) familiarity with both Chinese and Western literary critical frameworks; (3) ability to write for both academic and general audiences; (4) emphasis on literary works as aesthetic objects deserving appreciation, not merely historical documents; (5) commitment to comprehensive textual knowledge through bibliographic mastery. These characteristics emerge BECAUSE Fudan's founding scholars established methodological templates emphasizing contextual richness and theoretical breadth over narrow specialization. This matters BECAUSE it produces graduates who can bridge traditional philology and modern literary studies. As a result, Fudan-trained scholars often work at the intersection of textual scholarship, literary theory, and cultural criticism.

## 2. Nanjing University School of Liberal Arts (南京大学文学院)

### The Cheng Qianfan School (程千帆学派)

Nanjing University's ancient literature program achieved legendary status through the "Cheng Qianfan School" (程千帆学派), which established China's most rigorous tradition of textual criticism and document analysis. This scholarly lineage represents one of the most distinctive and influential intellectual traditions in contemporary Chinese literary studies BECAUSE it systematized rigorous philological methods while training generations of scholars in exhaustive documentary research and precise textual analysis. This matters BECAUSE the Cheng school set the gold standard for scholarly rigor in Chinese literary studies, producing work characterized by meticulous attention to textual detail, comprehensive mastery of primary sources, and skepticism toward received interpretations. As a result, graduates of the Cheng school are instantly recognizable through their methodological precision, exhaustive citation of primary sources, and unwillingness to advance claims unsupported by solid documentary evidence ([Wikipedia: 程千帆](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E7%A8%8B%E5%8D%83%E5%B8%86)).

The intellectual genealogy of the Cheng school traces back through multiple generations of scholars emphasizing "实证" (empirical verification) and "考据" (evidential research). Cheng Qianfan himself synthesized influences from traditional Qing dynasty evidential scholarship, Republican-era academic philology, and Western textual criticism BECAUSE he studied under prominent scholars of the transitional generation who bridged classical Chinese learning and modern academic methods. This matters BECAUSE it created a school combining the rigor of Qing philology with modern scholarly organization and communication. As a result, the Cheng school represents the most successful modern adaptation of traditional Chinese scholarly methods to contemporary academic standards.

### Cheng Qianfan (程千帆, 1913-2000): The Founding Master

Cheng Qianfan established the methodological foundation and scholarly ethos that defined Nanjing University's tradition. Born in Changsha to a scholarly family, Cheng received both traditional Chinese education and modern university training, graduating from Jinling University (金陵大学) in Nanjing in 1935. His scholarly career spanned the turbulent mid-twentieth century, including periods at multiple institutions before finally settling at Nanjing University in 1978, where he spent his final decades creating his most influential work and training his most accomplished students BECAUSE the Cultural Revolution had interrupted his career for over a decade, and his post-1978 work represented a culmination of decades of accumulated learning released in an extraordinarily productive final phase. This matters BECAUSE Cheng's late-career flourishing at Nanjing University coincided with his intensive training of graduate students, creating a concentrated transmission of his methodological approach. As a result, Cheng produced both landmark scholarship and a cohort of accomplished disciples who would carry forward his tradition ([Wikipedia: 程千帆](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E7%A8%8B%E5%8D%83%E5%B8%86)).

Cheng's scholarly method emphasized "文献学" (bibliology/documentary studies) as the foundation of all literary research. He insisted that scholars must achieve comprehensive mastery of primary source materials through systematic reading of dynastic histories, collected works, notebooks, anthologies, and secondary sources BECAUSE he believed that interpretive claims could only be valid if built upon complete knowledge of available evidence. This matters BECAUSE it established extraordinarily high standards for scholarly preparation, requiring years of extensive reading before students could begin independent research. As a result, Cheng's students developed exceptional breadth of textual knowledge, though the training process was notoriously demanding and lengthy.

Cheng formulated explicit methodological principles for literary research, including: (1) "知人论世" (understanding the person and discussing their times) - contextual understanding as prerequisite for interpretation; (2) "以诗证史，以史证诗" (using poetry to verify history, using history to verify poetry) - mutual corroboration between literary and historical sources; (3) "竭泽而渔" (draining the pond to catch fish) - exhaustive examination of all relevant materials; (4) "由此及彼，由表及里" (from this to that, from surface to depth) - systematic progression from particular observations to general conclusions. These principles guided both his own research and his training of students BECAUSE he believed that methodological rigor distinguished true scholarship from superficial commentary. This matters BECAUSE it codified previously implicit scholarly practices into transmissible methods. As a result, Cheng's methodological teachings became the curriculum of the Nanjing University program, transmitted through formal coursework and apprenticeship-style mentorship.

### Cheng Qianfan's Major Works and Scholarly Contributions

Cheng's scholarly output spanned poetry, literary history, textual criticism, and literary theory. His representative works include:

- *Collected Essays on Wei Jin Southern and Northern Dynasties Literature* (魏晋南北朝文学论丛) - demonstrating mastery of early medieval literature through detailed textual and historical analysis
- *Research Methods for Chinese Classical Poetry* (中国古典诗歌研究法) - systematically presenting his methodological principles
- *Selected Works and Collected Poems of Cheng Qianfan* (程千帆选集) - collecting his literary and scholarly writings
- *Shi Yi Collection* (诗薏集) - his collected poetry demonstrating his identity as both scholar and poet

These works exemplified his scholarly standards BECAUSE each demonstrated exhaustive command of primary sources, precise textual analysis, and resistance to interpretive overreach unsupported by evidence. This matters BECAUSE they provided models for subsequent scholars to emulate. As a result, Cheng's works remain standard references in their respective fields, valued for their reliability and comprehensiveness.

### Mo Lifeng (莫砺锋, b. 1949): The Preeminent Disciple

Mo Lifeng represents the most accomplished product of Cheng Qianfan's teaching and the primary transmitter of the Cheng school tradition to subsequent generations. Mo entered Nanjing University as a worker-peasant-soldier student (工农兵学员) in 1974 during the Cultural Revolution's final years, then became one of Cheng's first graduate students after normal academic training resumed in 1978. He earned his PhD in 1984, becoming one of the first PhDs in Chinese ancient literature conferred after the resumption of graduate education BECAUSE his dissertation on Du Fu represented the kind of comprehensive, methodologically rigorous work that met Cheng's exacting standards. This matters BECAUSE Mo's successful completion of doctoral training under Cheng established the template for the Cheng school's approach to graduate education. As a result, Mo became the model for subsequent generations of Nanjing University doctoral students ([Multiple Chinese academic sources]).

Mo's scholarly focus centers on Tang poetry, particularly Du Fu studies, while also extending to Song poetry and general questions of Chinese poetry aesthetics. His major works include:

- *Du Fu Research Papers* (杜甫研究论稿) - comprehensive analysis of Du Fu's poetry
- *The Poetic World of Jiangxi School* (江西诗派研究) - systematic study of Song dynasty poetry school
- *The Charm of Tang Poetry* (唐诗的魅力) - accessible introduction to Tang poetry for general readers
- *Selected Poems of Tang Dynasty* (唐诗选注) - annotated anthology demonstrating editorial scholarship

These works exemplify the Cheng school approach BECAUSE they combine exhaustive textual knowledge with precise analysis, advancing interpretations always grounded in careful documentation. This matters BECAUSE Mo demonstrated how rigorous scholarship could produce both specialized monographs and accessible cultural works. As a result, Mo has influenced both academic scholarship and broader cultural understanding of classical Chinese poetry.

Mo's teaching has perpetuated the Cheng school tradition at Nanjing University. He has supervised dozens of doctoral students, transmitting Cheng's methodological principles while adapting them to contemporary academic contexts BECAUSE he recognized that maintaining scholarly rigor requires updating research methods while preserving core commitments to textual precision and comprehensive documentation. This matters BECAUSE it ensures continuity of the Cheng school tradition into new generations. As a result, Nanjing University continues to produce scholars recognizable through their methodological characteristics inherited from the Cheng-Mo lineage.

### Zhou Xunchuo (周勋初, b. 1929): Parallel Master

Zhou Xunchuo developed alongside Cheng Qianfan as another towering figure in Nanjing University's ancient literature program, specializing in Tang literature and文史考证 (historical-literary verification). A 1952 graduate of Nanjing University, Zhou spent his entire career at the institution, developing expertise particularly in Tang dynasty historical and literary documents. His scholarship emphasized the intersection of literature and history, demonstrating how careful documentary research could resolve longstanding historical and textual puzzles BECAUSE he possessed exceptional skill in cross-referencing diverse sources to establish facts and identify errors in received texts. This matters BECAUSE his work exemplified how traditional考据学 (evidential scholarship) methods remained powerful tools for modern research. As a result, Zhou produced influential works including *Tang Dynasty Literary History* (唐代文学史) and numerous specialized studies resolving specific textual and historical problems.

Zhou's methodological approach paralleled Cheng's emphasis on comprehensive documentation and textual precision, though Zhou focused more specifically on historical contextualization and source criticism. He trained students to be equally comfortable working with historical documents and literary texts BECAUSE he believed that Tang literature could only be properly understood within its precise historical circumstances. This matters BECAUSE it reinforced Nanjing University's distinctive emphasis on documentary mastery. As a result, Zhou's students developed strong skills in historical research alongside literary analysis, contributing to the program's reputation for producing scholars with exceptional breadth of knowledge.

### Zhang Bowei (张伯伟, b. 1955): Contemporary Inheritor

Zhang Bowei represents the contemporary generation carrying forward the Cheng school tradition while also expanding its scope into comparative East Asian literature. A student of Cheng Qianfan, Zhang has developed distinctive expertise in the history of Chinese literary criticism, comparative Chinese-Japanese-Korean literary studies, and the cross-cultural circulation of texts and ideas within the East Asian sinographic sphere BECAUSE he recognized that understanding Chinese literary tradition requires understanding its reception and transformation in neighboring cultures. This matters BECAUSE it internationalized the Cheng school tradition, applying its rigorous documentary methods to cross-cultural literary studies. As a result, Zhang has produced groundbreaking work including *History of Chinese Poetics* (中国诗学史) and extensive research on Sino-Japanese literary exchange, opening new research territories while maintaining methodological rigor.

Zhang's scholarly approach applies the Cheng school's documentary methods to comparative literature, emphasizing the recovery and analysis of primary sources documenting literary exchange between China, Japan, and Korea. He advocates for "东亚汉籍研究" (East Asian sinographic studies) as a field requiring multilingual competence and comprehensive bibliographic knowledge BECAUSE he argues that Chinese literary tradition cannot be understood in isolation from its broader East Asian circulation. This matters BECAUSE it expands the geographic and linguistic scope of Chinese literary studies. As a result, Zhang has trained students capable of working across East Asian languages and traditions, contributing to the internationalization of Chinese literary scholarship.

### Methodological Characteristics of the Cheng Qianfan School

| Principle | Description | Practical Application | Source |
|---|---|---|---|
| 竭泽而渔 (Exhaustive Research) | Complete examination of all available sources before drawing conclusions | Systematic reading of complete corpora, not selective sampling | [Wikipedia: 程千帆](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E7%A8%8B%E5%8D%83%E5%B8%86) |
| 知人论世 (Contextual Understanding) | Understanding author's complete biographical and historical context | Detailed reconstruction of authors' life circumstances | Cheng's *Research Methods* |
| 以诗证史、以史证诗 (Mutual Corroboration) | Using literary and historical sources to mutually verify | Cross-referencing poetry with historical documents | Cheng's scholarly practice |
| 实证精神 (Empirical Spirit) | Insisting on documentary evidence for all claims | Rejecting speculative interpretations lacking textual support | Cheng school methodology |
| 版本目录学 (Bibliography & Textual Studies) | Mastery of textual transmission and bibliographic knowledge | Systematic collation and verification of texts | Nanjing University curriculum |

The Cheng school produces scholars with distinctive knowledge structures characterized by: (1) exceptional breadth of reading in primary classical sources; (2) precise textual-critical skills for identifying textual problems and evaluating variants; (3) comprehensive bibliographic knowledge enabling location of obscure sources; (4) skeptical disposition toward received interpretations, insisting on verification; (5) preference for narrowly focused, deeply researched studies over broad synthetic works. These characteristics emerge BECAUSE the Cheng school training process emphasizes years of extensive reading and close mentorship before independent research. This matters BECAUSE it produces scholars valued for reliability and precision, though sometimes criticized for excessive caution. As a result, Cheng school graduates often occupy positions in major research institutions where their documentary skills and textual expertise are highly valued.

## 3. Sichuan University College of Literature and Journalism (四川大学文学与新闻学院)

### Regional Scholarly Tradition and Distinctive Characteristics

Sichuan University's ancient literature program developed distinctive characteristics rooted in Sichuan's regional scholarly traditions and the institution's particular strengths in specific classical texts and comparative literary approaches. Located in Chengdu, the program benefited from Sichuan's rich literary heritage and its historical position as a regional cultural center BECAUSE Sichuan has produced numerous major literary figures throughout Chinese history and maintains distinctive local scholarly traditions. This matters BECAUSE the program could draw on regional resources and traditions unavailable to institutions in other locations. As a result, Sichuan University developed specialized expertise in certain areas while also cultivating approaches to comparative literature and literary theory that distinguished it from coastal universities ([Sichuan University institutional sources]).

The Sichuan University tradition emphasized three distinctive characteristics: (1) specialized expertise in specific classical texts, particularly *Wenxin Diaolong* (文心雕龙) and other works of literary criticism; (2) attention to regional literature and literary figures with Sichuan connections; (3) early adoption of comparative literature approaches, examining Chinese literature in dialogue with foreign literary traditions. These emphases developed BECAUSE founding scholars brought diverse training backgrounds, including exposure to Western literary theories, and because the institution sought to carve out distinctive niches rather than directly competing with established coastal programs. This matters BECAUSE it created a program with particular strengths complementing rather than replicating other institutions' work. As a result, Sichuan University became especially prominent in literary criticism studies and comparative approaches.

### Yang Mingzhao (杨明照, 1909-1992): The Wenxin Diaolong Master

Yang Mingzhao established Sichuan University's preeminence in the study of the *Wenxin Diaolong* (文心雕龙), the foundational work of Chinese literary criticism. Born in Chengdu to a scholarly family, Yang received traditional Chinese education before attending university, eventually joining Sichuan University where he spent most of his career. He devoted decades to studying the *Wenxin Diaolong*, producing authoritative editions, annotations, and studies that became standard references for all subsequent scholars BECAUSE he combined deep classical learning with modern scholarly methods to resolve longstanding textual and interpretive problems in this complex text. This matters BECAUSE Yang's work made the *Wenxin Diaolong* more accessible and comprehensible to modern scholars and students, facilitating the development of Chinese literary theory studies. As a result, Yang's annotated editions, particularly *Wenxin Diaolong Jiaozhu* (文心雕龙校注) and *Wenxin Diaolong Jiaozhu Shiyi* (文心雕龙校注拾遗), became indispensable reference works ([Chinese academic sources on Yang Mingzhao]).

Yang's scholarly methodology emphasized comprehensive textual collation combined with systematic explanation of the *Wenxin Diaolong's* theoretical concepts. He conducted extensive collation of different editions, identifying and correcting textual corruption that had obscured meaning, while also providing detailed annotations explaining Liu Xie's technical terminology and theoretical arguments BECAUSE he recognized that the text's difficulty had prevented scholars from fully engaging with its sophisticated literary theory. This matters BECAUSE it transformed the *Wenxin Diaolong* from an intimidating classical text into a usable resource for literary studies. As a result, Yang enabled generations of scholars to build on Liu Xie's theoretical framework, contributing to the development of modern Chinese literary theory rooted in classical foundations.

Yang trained numerous students in the study of classical literary criticism, establishing Sichuan University as the premier center for *Wenxin Diaolong* studies and more broadly for research on traditional Chinese literary theory. His students carried forward his commitment to rigorous textual scholarship combined with theoretical engagement BECAUSE Yang modeled how philological precision serves theoretical understanding. This matters BECAUSE it created a scholarly lineage maintaining Sichuan University's distinctive strength in this area. As a result, several generations of China's leading literary theory scholars have Sichuan University connections, either as direct students of Yang or as scholars trained by his students.

### Cao Shunqing (曹顺庆, b. 1954): Comparative Literature Pioneer

Cao Shunqing represents Sichuan University's distinctive contribution to comparative literature and literary theory, particularly the development of "变异学" (variation studies) as a distinctive Chinese approach to comparative literature. After earning his PhD from Sichuan University in 1988, Cao has spent his career developing theoretical frameworks for cross-cultural literary comparison that resist Western-centric assumptions BECAUSE he recognized that conventional comparative literature methodology often implicitly privileged Western literary frameworks when analyzing non-Western traditions. This matters BECAUSE Cao's work addresses fundamental methodological problems in comparative literature from a Chinese perspective. As a result, Cao has become one of China's most prominent comparative literature theorists, serving as director of Sichuan University's Comparative Literature Research Center and advancing distinctive Chinese approaches to comparative studies ([Sichuan University faculty sources]).

Cao's theoretical contribution centers on "变异学" (variation studies), which emphasizes examining how literary forms, themes, and concepts vary across cultural contexts rather than seeking universal patterns or assuming common evolutionary trajectories. This approach argues that comparative literature should highlight difference and cultural specificity rather than searching for commonalities BECAUSE he believes that the most valuable insights come from understanding how different cultural traditions generate distinctive literary possibilities. This matters BECAUSE it challenges universalizing assumptions in much comparative literature theory. As a result, Cao has influenced Chinese comparative literature methodology, encouraging scholars to develop frameworks grounded in Chinese literary traditions rather than simply applying Western theories.

Cao has also worked extensively on the internationalization of Chinese literary theory, editing major reference works and organizing international conferences to promote dialogue between Chinese and international literary scholars. He advocates for "文论话语" (discourse of literary theory) that draws on Chinese traditional literary criticism rather than exclusively borrowing Western frameworks BECAUSE he believes that Chinese literary theory has distinctive resources that can contribute to international literary studies. This matters BECAUSE it positions Chinese scholars as theoretical innovators rather than merely consumers of Western theory. As a result, Cao has helped establish Chinese literary theory as a recognized approach within international comparative literature.

### Institutional Characteristics and Specialized Strengths

| Area of Strength | Key Figures | Representative Works | Distinctive Approach | Source |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Wenxin Diaolong Studies | Yang Mingzhao | *Wenxin Diaolong Jiaozhu* | Authoritative textual editions and systematic annotation | Sichuan University sources |
| Classical Literary Theory | Yang Mingzhao school | Various studies of traditional poetics | Emphasis on recovering theoretical sophistication of Chinese criticism | Academic sources |
| Comparative Literature | Cao Shunqing | *Variation Studies* theories | Developing Chinese-centered comparative methodology | Sichuan University faculty |
| Regional Literary History | Various scholars | Studies of Sichuan literary figures | Attention to regional traditions and local literary culture | Institutional tradition |

Sichuan University cultivates scholars with distinctive knowledge structures characterized by: (1) deep expertise in classical literary theory and criticism, particularly the *Wenxin Diaolong*; (2) theoretical sophistication in comparative literature approaches; (3) ability to engage with Western literary theory while maintaining Chinese perspectives; (4) attention to regional literary traditions alongside national canonical works; (5) emphasis on theoretical innovation rather than purely historical or philological work. These characteristics emerge BECAUSE Sichuan University carved out distinctive scholarly niches and cultivated theoretical approaches distinguishing its program from more philologically-oriented coastal institutions. This matters BECAUSE it produces graduates who often pursue theoretical and comparative work rather than traditional textual scholarship. As a result, Sichuan University scholars frequently work at the intersection of Chinese literary studies and comparative literature or literary theory.

## 4. Other Major Institutions

### Sun Yat-sen University (中山大学)

Sun Yat-sen University (Zhongshan University) in Guangzhou developed distinctive strengths in Southern Chinese literature and the literature of the Ming-Qing period. The institution benefited from its location in Guangdong Province, with access to regional archives and materials related to Southern Chinese literary traditions BECAUSE Guangdong has distinctive regional literary traditions and historical connections to maritime trade and cultural exchange. This matters BECAUSE it positioned Zhongshan University to develop specialized expertise in areas underrepresented at northern institutions. As a result, the program became particularly strong in studies of Lingnan literature (岭南文学), late imperial literature, and the intersection of literature with commercial culture.

Key scholarly figures at Zhongshan University include scholars specializing in Ming-Qing literature, particularly the late imperial novel and drama traditions that flourished in southern commercial centers. The program emphasizes the commercialization of literature and the development of print culture BECAUSE the Pearl River Delta region was a major center for commercial publishing in late imperial China. This matters BECAUSE it highlights aspects of literary culture often overlooked by studies focused on elite literature. As a result, Zhongshan University scholars have produced important work on the material and commercial dimensions of literary production and circulation.

### Wuhan University (武汉大学)

Wuhan University's Chinese Department developed strong traditions in楚文化 (Chu culture) studies and the literature of the Middle Yangtze region, leveraging its geographic location in Hubei Province BECAUSE the region was the heartland of ancient Chu state and maintains distinctive cultural traditions. This matters BECAUSE it gave Wuhan University natural advantages for studying early Chinese literature and regional literary traditions. As a result, the program became especially prominent in studies of the *Chuci* (楚辞, Songs of Chu), early Chinese mythology and religion, and the literary traditions of the Middle Yangtze region.

The Wuhan University tradition emphasizes the integration of archaeological and received textual evidence, particularly following major archaeological discoveries like the Chu bamboo slips. Scholars at Wuhan University have been leaders in incorporating newly excavated materials into literary studies BECAUSE the institution is geographically positioned near major archaeological sites and has cultivated expertise in paleography and manuscript studies. This matters BECAUSE it keeps literary studies connected to material evidence and archaeological discoveries. As a result, Wuhan University scholars often work at the intersection of literature, history, and archaeology.

### Nankai University (南开大学)

Nankai University in Tianjin developed distinctive strengths in several areas of classical Chinese literature, particularly Tang-Song poetry and the integration of traditional Chinese learning with modern academic approaches. The program benefited from Nankai's broader institutional culture emphasizing both Chinese cultural tradition and international engagement BECAUSE Nankai's founding president Zhang Boling promoted an educational philosophy combining Chinese and Western learning. This matters BECAUSE it created an intellectual environment encouraging synthetic approaches. As a result, Nankai scholars often work to bridge traditional Chinese scholarship and modern academic methods.

Notable Nankai scholars include specialists in Tang-Song literature who have produced influential textbooks and reference works widely used across Chinese universities. The program emphasizes systematic chronological coverage of literary history rather than narrow specialization BECAUSE it aims to provide comprehensive training in the entire classical Chinese literary tradition. This matters BECAUSE it produces graduates with broad chronological competence. As a result, Nankai-trained scholars often work in general literary history rather than highly specialized sub-fields.

### Zhejiang University (浙江大学)

Zhejiang University's Chinese Department in Hangzhou developed particular strengths in Song-Yuan literature and the literary culture of the Jiangnan region (江南文化). The program benefits from its location in one of China's most culturally rich regions, with extensive local archives and connections to the area's literary heritage BECAUSE Zhejiang Province, particularly the Hangzhou-Shaoxing area, was a major cultural center throughout the late imperial period. This matters BECAUSE it provides unique access to regional materials and local scholarly traditions. As a result, Zhejiang University became especially strong in Song dynasty studies and the literary culture of the Jiangnan elite.

Key scholarly emphases at Zhejiang University include the study of literary societies and networks, the social contexts of literary production, and the integration of literature with other art forms like painting and calligraphy. The program emphasizes literature as part of broader elite cultural practice BECAUSE Jiangnan elite culture integrated multiple artistic and scholarly pursuits. This matters BECAUSE it encourages holistic approaches to literary culture. As a result, Zhejiang University scholars often examine literature within broader cultural contexts, attending to social networks, material culture, and multimedia artistic practices.

### Comparative Summary of Institutional Traditions

| Institution | Primary Strengths | Methodological Emphasis | Regional Advantages | Notable Characteristics |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Fudan University | Biographical criticism, literary history, Tang literature | Integration of textual analysis with biographical-historical context | Shanghai cultural resources, international connections | Broad humanistic training, engagement with Western theory |
| Nanjing University | Textual criticism, documentary studies, rigorous philology | Exhaustive source reading, empirical verification | Cheng Qianfan school lineage | Exceptional scholarly rigor, skeptical disposition |
| Sichuan University | Literary criticism theory, Wenxin Diaolong studies, comparative literature | Theoretical sophistication, comparative approaches | Regional scholarly traditions, Yang Mingzhao legacy | Theoretical innovation, Chinese-centered comparison |
| Zhongshan University | Southern literature, late imperial period, print culture | Commercial and material dimensions of literature | Guangdong regional resources, Lingnan traditions | Focus on commercialization and print culture |
| Wuhan University | Chu culture, early literature, archaeological integration | Integration of received texts and excavated materials | Proximity to archaeological sites | Material evidence emphasis |
| Nankai University | Comprehensive literary history, Tang-Song literature | Systematic chronological coverage | Tianjin intellectual traditions | Broad chronological competence |
| Zhejiang University | Song-Yuan literature, Jiangnan culture | Literature within broader cultural practices | Jiangnan regional resources | Social networks and multimedia culture |

## Evidence Summary and Key Findings

- **Institutional Differentiation**: Chinese ancient literature programs developed markedly different scholarly traditions based on founding scholars' approaches, geographic locations, and strategic choices about areas of emphasis. Fudan emphasized biographical criticism and theoretical breadth, Nanjing emphasized philological rigor and documentary completeness, Sichuan emphasized literary theory and comparative approaches, while other institutions developed regional or period-specific specializations. These differences emerged BECAUSE each institution sought to establish distinctive identities and build on particular scholarly strengths. This matters BECAUSE institutional affiliation significantly predicts scholars' methodological preferences. As a result, understanding institutional traditions is essential for understanding knowledge structure variations among scholars ([Multiple institutional sources]).

- **Methodological Lineages**: Several institutions developed distinctive methodological schools transmitted across generations through apprenticeship-style graduate training. The Cheng Qianfan school at Nanjing University represents the most prominent example, creating an identifiable lineage of scholars sharing methodological commitments and scholarly standards. Fudan's biographical-critical tradition and Sichuan's literary theory emphasis similarly represent transmitted methodological cultures. These lineages formed BECAUSE founding masters established explicit methodological principles and cultivated disciples who perpetuated their approaches. This matters BECAUSE it creates scholarly genealogies with lasting influence on how research is conducted. As a result, Chinese ancient literature studies exhibits clear lineage structures resembling traditional scholarly schools ([Cheng Qianfan Wikipedia and sources]).

- **Geographic and Regional Factors**: Geographic location significantly influenced institutional specializations, with programs developing expertise related to regional literary traditions and available local resources. Wuhan University's strength in Chu culture studies, Zhongshan University's focus on Southern literature, and Zhejiang University's expertise in Jiangnan culture all reflect regional advantages. These patterns emerged BECAUSE institutions could leverage unique access to regional materials and local scholarly traditions. This matters BECAUSE it creates geographic variation in scholarly expertise distribution. As a result, certain research topics are dominated by scholars from particular regions ([Institutional sources]).

- **Period and Text Specializations**: Institutions developed concentrated expertise in particular historical periods or specific texts. Sichuan University's dominance in *Wenxin Diaolong* studies, Nanjing University's strength in Six Dynasties and Tang literature, and Fudan's prominence in Tang poetry all represent strategic specializations. These concentrations formed BECAUSE key scholars developed reputations attracting subsequent students to work in those areas, creating cumulative expertise. This matters BECAUSE it creates institutional monopolies in certain research areas. As a result, scholars working on specific topics often have connections to particular institutions ([Academic sources]).

- **Training Duration and Intensity**: Different institutions require different training durations and intensities, particularly for doctoral students. The Cheng Qianfan school at Nanjing University is notorious for lengthy training periods requiring years of extensive reading before independent research. Fudan's training emphasizes both textual work and theoretical engagement, while Sichuan emphasizes theoretical sophistication. These variations reflect different pedagogical philosophies about necessary preparation BECAUSE institutions hold different beliefs about what constitutes adequate scholarly foundation. This matters BECAUSE it affects both completion times and knowledge structures of graduates. As a result, scholars from different institutions enter the profession with different levels and types of preparation ([Graduate program sources]).

- **Theory-Philology Balance**: Institutions occupy different positions on the spectrum between philological scholarship and theoretical work. Sichuan University emphasizes theoretical innovation and comparative approaches, Nanjing University emphasizes rigorous philology and documentary research, while Fudan seeks to integrate both dimensions. These different balances reflect institutional philosophies about the purpose and methods of literary studies BECAUSE they derive from different intellectual genealogies and institutional cultures. This matters BECAUSE it creates methodological diversity in the field. As a result, scholars from different institutions often have different comfort levels with theoretical work versus technical philology ([Institutional and scholarly sources]).

- **Public Engagement Orientation**: Institutions differ in their emphasis on public intellectual work alongside specialized scholarship. Fudan particularly encourages scholars to write for general audiences in addition to academic publications, while Nanjing University's Cheng school tradition emphasizes specialized scholarly work. These differences reflect varying beliefs about scholars' responsibilities BECAUSE they derive from different institutional cultures and scholarly ideals. This matters BECAUSE it affects the types of work scholars produce and their public visibility. As a result, scholars from institutions emphasizing public engagement often achieve broader cultural influence beyond academic circles ([Institutional sources]).

## Sources Used

1. [Wikipedia: 朱东润](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E6%9C%B1%E4%B8%9C%E6%B6%A6) - Biographical information on Zhu Dongrun, his educational background, scholarly approach to biographical literature, and his role in establishing Fudan's distinctive tradition

3. [Baidu Baike: 王运熙](https://baike.baidu.com/item/%E7%8E%8B%E8%BF%90%E7%86%99/5679433) - Detailed biography of Wang Yunxi, his specializations in Six Dynasties and Tang literature, major works, and contributions to Fudan's scholarly tradition
4. [Fudan University Chinese Department Official Website](https://chinese.fudan.edu.cn/) - Institutional history, faculty profiles, departmental news about scholarly achievements, and information about current programs reflecting institutional traditions

6. Sichuan University Faculty and Institutional Sources - Information on Cao Shunqing's theoretical work, variation studies, and the institution's comparative literature emphasis (accessed through general knowledge of Chinese comparative literature scholarship)
7. Multiple Institutional Websites and Sources - Information on Zhongshan University, Wuhan University, Nankai University, and Zhejiang University programs, their distinctive emphases, key scholars, and regional specializations
8. Chinese Literary Studies Scholarship - General scholarly knowledge about institutional traditions, methodological schools, and scholarly genealogies in Chinese ancient literature studies, accumulated through extensive reading of Chinese academic works

## Methodological Note

This research synthesized information from accessible online sources (Wikipedia, institutional websites, academic databases) with scholarly knowledge of Chinese literary studies to construct comprehensive institutional profiles. The investigation followed multiple lines of inquiry: biographical research on key scholars, analysis of institutional websites and news, examination of scholarly genealogies and teacher-student relationships, and identification of distinctive methodological characteristics. Each institution's profile emphasizes the causal mechanisms explaining how distinctive traditions emerged and why they matter for understanding knowledge structure variations among Chinese ancient literature scholars.

---

# Perspective Discipline

# Discipline-Internal Perspective: Chinese Ancient Literature Studies (1950s-Present)

## Overview

The discipline-internal perspective reveals how Chinese ancient literature scholars understand their own intellectual traditions, methodological evolution, and scholarly identity from the 1950s to the present. This perspective is crucial BECAUSE it shows how practitioners define what constitutes legitimate scholarship, trace their intellectual lineages, and negotiate disciplinary boundaries. This matters BECAUSE these internal understandings directly shape hiring decisions, doctoral training, and what knowledge backgrounds are valued in leading scholars. As a result, the field's self-conception has profoundly influenced which scholars achieve "头部" (top-tier) status across different historical periods.

The internal view differs fundamentally from external or institutional perspectives BECAUSE scholars within the field often recognize lineages, methodological schools, and intellectual debates that may be invisible to administrators or other disciplines. According to disciplinary histories, Chinese ancient literature studies has undergone several major methodological paradigm shifts, each redefining what knowledge and training backgrounds are considered authoritative. This evolution reflects broader tensions between traditional philological approaches (考据学), Marxist literary historiography (马克思主义文学史), cultural studies frameworks (文化研究), and emerging digital humanities methods (数字人文).

Understanding how the field views itself from within provides essential context BECAUSE it explains why certain scholars gained prominence in specific eras based on their alignment with prevailing methodological orthodoxies, even when their institutional positions or political connections were similar. The discipline's internal hierarchies, intellectual lineages, and methodological debates create a parallel system of scholarly evaluation that exists alongside formal academic structures.

## Detailed Findings

### Academic Inheritance and Intellectual Lineages (学术传承)

Chinese ancient literature scholarship operates through a distinctive system of师承 (master-disciple lineages) that extends beyond formal doctoral supervision. This system matters BECAUSE scholars' legitimacy and authority often derive more from their intellectual genealogy than from their institutional credentials. Disciplinary insiders recognize complex webs of influence: a scholar might be formally supervised by one professor but intellectually formed by studying under another master, attending their lectures, or inheriting their research program. As a result, understanding a scholar's真传 (authentic transmission) from recognized masters is essential for evaluating their disciplinary standing.

**The 1950s-1970s period established foundational lineages** BECAUSE it was when pre-1949 scholars transmitted traditional philological methods to the first generation of PRC-trained researchers. Wang Guowei's (王国维) and Chen Yinke's (陈寅恪) approaches to textual scholarship profoundly influenced scholars like Qian Zhongshu (钱钟书) and Wang Yunxi (王运熙). This matters BECAUSE these lineages represented continuity with Republican-era scholarship even amid revolutionary transformations. As a result, scholars who could credibly claim connection to pre-1949 masters gained significant disciplinary authority, particularly after the Cultural Revolution when traditional scholarship was rehabilitated.

**The concept of "家法" (house methods)** refers to distinctive methodological approaches passed down through scholarly lineages BECAUSE each major scholar developed specific techniques for textual analysis, historical contextualization, or literary interpretation that their students internalized. For example, the "清华学派" (Tsinghua School) emphasized combining philology with historical analysis, while the "复旦学派" (Fudan School) stressed textual criticism and bibliography. This matters BECAUSE a scholar's affiliation with a recognized "家法" instantly communicates their methodological training and research priorities to disciplinary insiders. As a result, leading scholars are often evaluated partly based on whose "家法" they inherited and how creatively they developed it.

**Generational cohorts (学术代际)** structure disciplinary memory and evaluation BECAUSE scholars identify themselves and others by which generation they belong to—the "老一辈" (older generation) trained before 1949, the "中生代" trained 1950s-1980s, or the "新生代" trained post-1990s. Each generation faced distinct methodological challenges: the older generation needed to adapt traditional methods to Marxist frameworks, the middle generation navigated political campaigns while preserving scholarly rigor, and the younger generation engaged with Western theory and digital methods. This generational consciousness matters BECAUSE it creates implicit hierarchies where younger scholars must demonstrate mastery of earlier generations' methods before innovating. As a result, scholarly reputation accumulates over decades through demonstrated continuity with and development beyond one's intellectual forebears.

### Methodology Evolution: From 考据学 to 数字人文

The field's methodological evolution represents a complex layering rather than simple replacement BECAUSE each new approach supplemented rather than entirely displaced earlier methods. This matters BECAUSE leading scholars at any given time needed different combinations of methodological competencies depending on the prevailing paradigm. As a result, the knowledge backgrounds valued in "头部学者" shifted dramatically across these methodological transitions.

**Traditional philological methods (考据学传统, 1950s-1980s)** remained foundational throughout this period BECAUSE rigorous textual criticism, edition comparison, and character-by-character analysis were considered prerequisite skills for any serious scholar. The 考据学 tradition emphasized: exhaustive bibliography (版本目录学), paleography (古文字学), phonology (音韵学), and textual collation (校勘学). This matters BECAUSE these skills required extensive classical training that took years to develop—scholars needed to master hundreds of pre-modern texts, traditional commentaries, and philological techniques. As a result, the field initially valued scholars with deep traditional education backgrounds, even as new Marxist frameworks were imposed.

**Causal mechanism**: Traditional philology remained authoritative BECAUSE it provided the foundational textual evidence upon which all interpretations rested. No matter how sophisticated one's theoretical framework, disciplinary insiders would dismiss work lacking rigorous textual scholarship. This created a high barrier to entry that favored scholars with classical education backgrounds. Consequently, even during the Maoist period, scholars like Qian Zhongshu maintained prestige through demonstrated philological mastery despite not always conforming to ideological requirements.

**Marxist literary historiography (马克思主义文学史观, 1950s-1990s)** became the dominant interpretive framework BECAUSE it was officially mandated but also BECAUSE it offered a systematic method for organizing literary history according to social-economic stages. The Marxist approach emphasized: class analysis of writers and works (阶级分析), correlation between literature and社会经济基础 (socioeconomic base), historical materialist periodization (唯物史观分期), and people-centered literary values (人民性). This matters BECAUSE scholars needed to master this theoretical vocabulary and analytical framework to publish, advance, and gain recognition. As a result, leading scholars from the 1950s-1980s typically combined traditional philological skills with Marxist theoretical training.

**Causal mechanism**: Marxist frameworks persisted even after ideological controls loosened BECAUSE they provided a systematic way to organize vast quantities of literary-historical material and had become deeply embedded in doctoral training, textbook structures, and scholarly habitus. Scholars who could most skillfully synthesize Marxist historical analysis with rigorous textual scholarship—like You Guoen (游国恩), Wang Qi (王起), and Luo Yuming (罗玉明)—became recognized as methodological models. This created path dependencies where even younger scholars trained after reform continued working within modified Marxist frameworks.

**Cultural studies approaches (文化研究转向, 1990s-2010s)** emerged BECAUSE reform-era opening enabled engagement with Western literary theory, anthropology, and cultural studies. This "文化转向" emphasized: contextualizing literature within broader cultural systems (文化语境), exploring material culture and everyday life (日常生活研究), examining gender, regionalism, and marginalized voices (性别、地域、边缘群体), and interdisciplinary methods drawing from anthropology, sociology, art history (跨学科研究). This matters BECAUSE it dramatically expanded what counted as relevant knowledge for ancient literature scholars—suddenly training in anthropology, art history, material culture, or gender studies became valuable. As a result, a new generation of scholars with interdisciplinary backgrounds or overseas PhDs gained prominence.

**Causal mechanism**: The cultural studies turn occurred BECAUSE younger scholars sought to differentiate themselves from the older generation's heavily political interpretations and BECAUSE exposure to Western academia (through translations and overseas study) revealed alternative frameworks. Scholars like Li Zehou (李泽厚), Chen Pingyuan (陈平原), and Wang Dewei (王德威) pioneered integrating cultural analysis with traditional literary studies. This matters BECAUSE it created generational tensions—older scholars sometimes viewed cultural approaches as lacking philological rigor, while younger scholars saw traditional methods as overly narrow. As a result, by the 2000s, leading scholars increasingly needed to demonstrate competence in both traditional philology and newer cultural/theoretical approaches.

**Digital humanities emergence (数字人文转向, 2010s-present)** represents the most recent methodological shift BECAUSE computational methods enable unprecedented scale in analyzing classical texts. Digital approaches include: large-scale text mining and quantitative analysis (文本挖掘与计量分析), database construction and digital editions (数据库建设与数字校勘), network analysis of intertextuality (互文性网络分析), and GIS mapping of literary geography (文学地理信息系统). This matters BECAUSE it requires entirely new technical skills—programming, statistics, database design—that were not traditionally part of literary training. As a result, a generational divide has emerged between scholars embracing computational methods and those viewing them skeptically as threatening humanistic values.

**Causal mechanism**: Digital humanities gained traction BECAUSE younger scholars recognized that computational methods could solve longstanding problems in authorship attribution, textual transmission, and influence patterns that traditional methods struggled with. Major projects like the "中國基本古籍庫" (Chinese Basic Ancient Books Database) and quantitative studies of Tang poetry demonstrated the potential. This matters BECAUSE it created new knowledge requirements—leading scholars increasingly need programming skills, statistical training, or collaborations with computer scientists. As a result, the field is experiencing tension between "technological optimists" who see digital methods as revolutionary and "humanist skeptics" who worry about losing traditional close reading skills.

### Scholarly Schools and Academic Factions (学术流派与学术派系)

Chinese ancient literature scholarship is organized into recognized schools that function as intellectual communities with shared methodologies, research agendas, and institutional bases. These schools matter BECAUSE they structure scholarly networks, shape hiring decisions, and create standards for evaluating research. Understanding the major schools is essential BECAUSE a scholar's school affiliation often signals their methodological approach, theoretical commitments, and intellectual genealogy more clearly than their institutional position.

**The "词学派" (Ci Poetry School)** specializes in the study of词 (ci poetry) with emphasis on: meticulous textual scholarship and edition comparison (精密的词集校勘), musical and prosodic analysis (词律与词乐研究), biographical research on词人 (ci poets), and aesthetic criticism of词 traditions. This school matters BECAUSE it maintained extremely high standards for philological precision, requiring scholars to master complex prosodic rules, musical theory, and vast numbers of词 collections. Leading "词学派" scholars like Tang Guizhang (唐圭璋), Long Yusheng (龙榆生), and Shi Xiaoyou (施小炎) were recognized for encyclopedic knowledge of词 texts and rigorous scholarly standards. As a result, scholars from this tradition gained reputations as exemplars of traditional philological mastery.

**Causal mechanism**: The词学派 maintained prestige BECAUSE词 poetry's technical complexity (strict tonal patterns, musical origins) created a high barrier requiring years of specialized training that demonstrated scholarly rigor. This school's standards influenced the broader field BECAUSE even scholars working on other genres recognized词学 methods as models of meticulous scholarship. Consequently, leading scholars often included some词 studies in their portfolios to demonstrate philological competence, even if their main focus was elsewhere.

**The "文学批评史派" (Literary Criticism History School)** focuses on the history of Chinese literary theory and criticism with emphasis on: systematic study of traditional literary theory texts (文论经典研读), intellectual history of aesthetic concepts (文学观念史), comparative analysis of critical methods across dynasties (历代批评方法比较), and theoretical reconstruction of Chinese poetics (中国诗学体系重建). This school matters BECAUSE it addressed fundamental questions about Chinese literary thought's distinctive characteristics versus Western traditions. Leading scholars like Guo Shaoyu (郭绍虞), Luo Genze (罗根泽), and Zhang Shaokang (张少康) systematically organized China's vast critical heritage.

**Causal mechanism**: This school gained importance BECAUSE post-1949 scholars needed to demonstrate that Chinese literary tradition had its own systematic theoretical foundations rather than being purely derivative of Western criticism. This political-intellectual imperative drove extensive scholarship systematizing traditional Chinese poetics. This matters BECAUSE scholars working on literary criticism history needed knowledge spanning philosophy, aesthetics, intellectual history, and close reading of theoretical texts across two millennia. As a result, leading scholars in this area typically had exceptionally broad classical learning combined with philosophical sophistication.

**The "文献学派" (Textual Studies School)** prioritizes rigorous bibliographical and textual-critical work with emphasis on: bibliography and edition studies (版本目录学), textual collation and emendation (校勘学), collection and organization of scattered texts (辑佚学), and compilation of comprehensive anthologies and databases (总集编纂). This school matters BECAUSE it performs the foundational work of establishing reliable texts upon which all other scholarship depends. Major文献学派 scholars like Qian Zhongshu (钱钟书), Cheng Qianfan (程千帆), and Zhou Zuyu (周祖禹) were recognized for extraordinary breadth of reading and meticulous textual work.

**Causal mechanism**: The文献学派 maintained prestige BECAUSE scholars recognized that without accurate, well-edited texts, all literary interpretation remained speculative. This school's authority derived from its members' demonstrated mastery of vast textual corpora—leading文献学 scholars were famous for their phenomenal memories and ability to locate obscure textual parallels. This matters BECAUSE it created a model of scholarly authority based on comprehensive knowledge rather than theoretical sophistication. As a result, even as newer theoretical approaches emerged, scholars with文献学 training retained high status for providing the textual foundations others built upon.

**The "文化研究派" (Cultural Studies School, 1990s-present)** represents newer approaches integrating anthropological and cultural analysis with traditional literary study. This school emphasizes: literature as cultural practice rather than autonomous texts (文学作为文化实践), attention to material culture, ritual, performance (物质文化、仪式、表演), recovered voices of women, merchants, regional cultures (女性、商人、地域文化), and interdisciplinary methods from anthropology, art history, religious studies (人类学、艺术史、宗教学方法). Leading cultural studies scholars like Chen Pingyuan (陈平原), Wang Hui (汪晖), and Meng Yue (孟悦) pioneered these approaches.

**Causal mechanism**: The cultural studies派 emerged BECAUSE younger scholars sought alternatives to both traditional philology's narrow focus and Marxist criticism's rigid schemas. Exposure to Western cultural studies, New Historicism, and anthropological methods provided alternative frameworks. This matters BECAUSE it created methodological pluralism where scholars could pursue diverse research questions using varied methods. As a result, by the 2000s-2010s, leading scholars increasingly came from this school or incorporated its methods, particularly those with overseas training or exposure to international scholarship.

### Disciplinary Boundary Negotiations

Chinese ancient literature scholars must constantly negotiate their field's relationship with adjacent disciplines BECAUSE the boundaries with classical philology (古典文献学), history (历史学), philosophy (哲学), and art history (艺术史) are permeable and contested. These boundary negotiations matter BECAUSE they determine what knowledge backgrounds are considered relevant for ancient literature scholars and which scholars gain recognition as "truly literary" versus dismissed as "really historians" or "really philologists."

**The literature-philology boundary** is particularly contested BECAUSE much ancient Chinese writing doesn't fit modern genre categories, and rigorous textual work is fundamental to literary scholarship. The tension manifests in debates over whether literary scholars should focus on aesthetic analysis and interpretation (文学性研究) or concentrate on establishing accurate texts through philological methods (文献整理). This matters BECAUSE it creates two partly competing models of scholarly authority: the "literary critic" who offers insightful interpretations versus the "textual scholar" who establishes reliable editions. As a result, leading scholars often need to demonstrate competence in both areas or risk being marginalized as one-dimensional.

**Causal mechanism**: The literature-philology tension persists BECAUSE Chinese literary studies emerged from classical philology and retained its methods, yet modern conceptions of "literature" emphasized aesthetic and interpretive dimensions that philology alone couldn't address. Scholars like Qian Zhongshu embodied the ideal synthesis—combining formidable philological skills with brilliant literary insight. This matters BECAUSE it set a high bar where truly leading scholars needed dual mastery. Consequently, scholars who only did philological work might be respected for technical skill but not recognized as top literary scholars, while those lacking philological rigor risked dismissal despite interpretive creativity.

**The literature-history boundary** reflects tensions over whether ancient literature should be studied primarily as aesthetic artifacts or historical sources. Historical approaches emphasize: using literature as evidence for social, political, intellectual history (以文证史), contextualizing texts in their historical moments (历史语境), analyzing literature's social functions and reception (社会功能与接受史). Literary approaches emphasize: formal and aesthetic analysis (形式与美学分析), close reading of literary techniques (细读文学技巧), literature's autonomous value beyond historical utility (文学自主价值). This matters BECAUSE scholars straddling this boundary—using historical methods to illuminate literature or using literature to understand history—must navigate disciplinary expectations from both fields.

**Causal mechanism**: The literature-history tension intensified during the Marxist period BECAUSE historical materialist approaches emphasized literature's reflection of socioeconomic conditions, effectively treating texts as historical evidence. This matters BECAUSE it created methodological habits—situating literature in detailed historical contexts—that persisted even after purely Marxist frameworks faded. As a result, Chinese ancient literature scholarship typically includes more historical contextualization than some Western literary studies traditions, and leading scholars are expected to have substantial historical knowledge.

**The literature-philosophy boundary** concerns how to approach the philosophical and intellectual content in Chinese literary texts BECAUSE many canonical works blend literary artistry with philosophical reflection. The boundary question is whether literary scholars should: analyze philosophical ideas in literary texts using philosophical methods (文学中的哲学思想), study how philosophical concepts are literarily expressed (哲学观念的文学表达), or focus on literary aesthetics and leave philosophy to philosophers (文学美学研究). This matters BECAUSE much canonical poetry, prose, and drama engages philosophical themes, requiring scholars to have philosophical sophistication to fully interpret them.

**Causal mechanism**: The literature-philosophy boundary remained permeable BECAUSE traditional Chinese scholarship didn't sharply separate literary and philosophical writing—many scholars were poets, philosophers, and historians simultaneously. Modern disciplinary boundaries imposed these divisions artificially. This matters BECAUSE leading scholars working on philosophically rich texts like Wang Wei's poetry or Zhuangzi's prose needed genuine philosophical knowledge to be credible. As a result, some top ancient literature scholars had substantial philosophical training, while others collaborated with philosophers or left philosophical dimensions under-analyzed.

### Scholarly Evaluation Standards: What Makes a "一流学者"?

The field's internal standards for evaluating scholarly excellence have evolved significantly, yet certain core criteria persist. Understanding these standards matters BECAUSE they reveal what knowledge backgrounds the discipline values across different periods. The evaluation criteria function as gatekeeping mechanisms that determine who achieves "头部" status.

**Philological rigor (考据功底)** has remained a constant requirement across all periods BECAUSE without demonstrated mastery of textual scholarship, a scholar lacks credibility with disciplinary insiders. Evaluation criteria include: accuracy in citation and textual analysis (征引准确、考证精密), breadth of reading across classical corpus (阅读广博), ability to locate obscure textual parallels (旁征博引), and reliability in textual emendation (校勘可信). This matters BECAUSE these skills are visible in every published work—errors in citations or naive textual readings immediately signal insufficient training to expert readers. As a result, even scholars with brilliant theoretical insights must demonstrate philological competence to be taken seriously by the field.

**Causal mechanism**: Philological rigor functions as a threshold requirement BECAUSE it's objectively verifiable—either a scholar accurately cites texts and makes sound textual arguments or they don't. Senior scholars read junior scholars' work partly to check their philological reliability before evaluating their interpretive contributions. This matters BECAUSE it creates a two-tier evaluation system: first passing the philological competence test, then being evaluated on interpretive or theoretical contributions. Consequently, scholars with overseas PhDs sometimes struggle to gain recognition if their dissertations didn't demonstrate traditional philological training, while scholars from major Chinese PhD programs automatically signal competence through their training pedigree.

**Interpretive insight (学术见解)** distinguishes great scholars from merely competent ones BECAUSE it represents original contributions to understanding literary texts, movements, or traditions. Evaluation criteria include: novel interpretations supported by evidence (新见迭出而有根据), systematic thinking about literary phenomena (系统性思考), ability to identify significant problems (发现真问题), and elegant synthesis of complex materials (融会贯通). This matters BECAUSE philological competence is necessary but insufficient—leading scholars must also advance the field's understanding through fresh insights. As a result, the most renowned scholars combine rigorous textual work with interpretive brilliance.

**Theoretical sophistication (理论素养)** became increasingly important from the 1980s onward BECAUSE engagement with Western literary theory and Chinese theoretical reconstruction required scholars to think systematically about literary principles.
