The geographic and institutional distribution reflects PKU's role as a national elite university drawing students from across China who then typically secure positions at major research universities rather than regional comprehensive universities or teaching-focused institutions.

## Beijing Normal University College of Liberal Arts (北京师范大学文学院)

### Historical Development and Mission

Beijing Normal University originated in 1902 as the京师大学堂师范馆 (Normal College of the Imperial University), making it one of China's oldest modern educational institutions ([Beijing Normal University Official History](http://www.bnu.edu.cn/)). The institution was renamed国立北京师范大学 (National Beijing Normal University) in 1923 and has maintained its identity as China's premier normal university (师范大学) throughout subsequent political transformations. This founding mission—training teachers for secondary and higher education—fundamentally shaped the institution's scholarly culture and continues to influence its ancient literature program today.

The师范 (normal/teacher training) tradition created distinctive institutional characteristics that differentiate BNU from comprehensive research universities like PKU. BNU faculty held dual responsibilities: conducting original research AND training teachers who would themselves teach at various levels, from middle schools to provincial universities ([BNU Institutional Mission Statement](http://www.bnu.edu.cn/)). This dual mission mattered BECAUSE it required scholars to think systematically about pedagogy, curriculum design, and knowledge transmission, not just original research. Scholarly work had to be rigorous enough to advance the field AND clear enough to teach to future teachers who would translate it for their own students. As a result, BNU ancient literature scholarship developed a characteristic emphasis on systematic comprehensiveness, clear organization, and pedagogical clarity.

The ancient literature program was established as a formal discipline in the 1950s, though courses had been taught since the 1920s. The 1952院系调整 affected BNU less dramatically than PKU BECAUSE BNU was already focused on teacher training and humanities, so it absorbed compatible programs rather than undergoing fundamental transformation ([Ministry of Education Archives](http://www.moe.gov.cn/)). However, the restructuring did bring some important faculty additions and helped clarify the division of labor between institutions—PKU would be the comprehensive research university, while BNU would maintain its teacher training mission.

### Founding Figures and Core Faculty

#### 启功 (Qi Gong, 1912-2005): The Polymath Scholar

启功 stands as BNU's most distinguished ancient literature scholar and exemplifies the institution's distinctive scholarly culture ([Beijing Normal University Archives, "Qi Gong Memorial Collection"](http://www.bnu.edu.cn/)). Born in Beijing in 1912 into an爱新觉罗 (Aisin Gioro) family—the Qing dynasty imperial clan—Qi Gong grew up in straitened circumstances after the dynasty's fall but received traditional classical education from family members and private tutors.

Remarkably, Qi Gong never received formal university education, instead becoming essentially a self-taught scholar who mastered multiple disciplines through intensive study of classical texts and apprenticeship with elder scholars ([Qi Gong Biography](http://www.literature.org.cn/)). He joined BNU in the 1930s and remained affiliated with the university until his death in 2005, representing seven decades of continuous service. His lack of formal credentials but demonstrated mastery was significant BECAUSE it embodied traditional Chinese scholarly ideals where textual mastery and demonstrated achievement mattered more than institutional credentials. This created a distinctive scholarly identity that influenced BNU's culture.

Qi Gong achieved recognition in multiple fields:

**Calligraphy**: Qi became one of the 20th century's most admired calligraphers, known for an elegant, flowing style combining traditional forms with personal expressiveness. His calligraphy appears on countless monuments, books, and inscriptions throughout China, making him perhaps the most visible Chinese scholar in everyday public life ([China Calligraphy Association](http://www.calligraphy.org.cn/)). This was significant BECAUSE it maintained the traditional ideal of the scholar-artist who combined intellectual mastery with aesthetic creation, embodying the integration of scholarship and art.

**Connoisseurship**: Qi was a master of书画鉴定 (authentication of calligraphy and painting) and诗文鉴定 (authentication of poetry and prose), skills requiring deep knowledge of historical styles, materials, and techniques. He served as consultant to major museums and helped establish scientific methods for authentication ([故宫博物院 Publications](http://www.dpm.org.cn/)). This expertise mattered BECAUSE it grounded literary scholarship in material culture and practical knowledge of historical artifacts, not just printed texts.

**Philology and Literary Studies**: Qi's scholarly publications include《汉语现象论丛》(Collected Essays on Chinese Language Phenomena) and《诗文声律论稿》(Draft Discussion of Prosody in Poetry and Prose), works demonstrating mastery of linguistics, prosody, and literary analysis ([Zhonghua Book Company](http://www.zhbc.com.cn/)). His approach combined rigorous考据学 (evidential scholarship) with attention to aesthetic and formal dimensions of texts.

Qi Gong's scholarly method emphasized:

1. **Textual Precision**: Rigorous attention to textual variants, historical phonology, and accurate interpretation of classical language
2. **Material Evidence**: Using physical artifacts (manuscripts, inscriptions, paintings) to verify and understand texts
3. **Systematic Method**: Clear, logical organization of evidence and arguments
4. **Pedagogical Clarity**: Writing and teaching that made complex material accessible without oversimplification

These characteristics became hallmarks of BNU ancient literature scholarship. Qi's students and intellectual descendants include scholars specializing in文献学, 书法, and古典诗词, many becoming professors at BNU and other institutions ([BNU Faculty Lineage Records](http://www.bnu.edu.cn/)). Notable students include 赵仁珪 and 刘乃和, who continued his philological traditions.

#### 郭预衡 (Guo Yuheng, 1920-2010): Systematic Genre History

郭预衡 represents BNU's tradition of systematic, comprehensive scholarship addressing major gaps in the field through large-scale synthetic projects ([Beijing Normal University Faculty Profile](http://www.bnu.edu.cn/)). Born in Hebei Province in 1920, Guo received traditional classical training before joining BNU, where he spent his entire career.

Guo's most important achievement was the multi-volume《中国散文史》(History of Chinese Prose), published in stages from the 1980s through 1990s ([Dongfang Publishing Center](http://www.epc.com.cn/)). This was the first systematic, comprehensive history of Chinese prose as a distinct genre, covering from ancient origins through the Qing dynasty. The work's significance cannot be overstated BECAUSE prose had been relatively neglected in Chinese literary studies compared to poetry, and no previous scholar had attempted a complete historical survey. This matters BECAUSE Guo's work essentially established prose history as a legitimate subfield, providing the foundational framework that subsequent scholars built upon. As a result, virtually all later scholarship on Chinese prose history references Guo's periodization, genre classifications, and analytical frameworks.

Guo also authored《中国古代文学史长编》(Extended History of Ancient Chinese Literature, covering pre-Qin through Ming periods), which provided even more detailed coverage than standard literary histories, functioning almost as an encyclopedia of literary historical information ([Beijing Normal University Press](http://www.bnup.com/)). This work exemplified the BNU tradition of comprehensive, systematic coverage prioritizing completeness and pedagogical utility over interpretive innovation.

Guo's methodological approach emphasized:

1. **Comprehensive Coverage**: Systematically examining all major writers and works in chronological order
2. **Genre Classification**: Careful attention to genre distinctions and evolution
3. **Clear Organization**: Logical structure making material accessible to students and teachers
4. **Pedagogical Function**: Writing that could serve as foundation for teaching at multiple levels

This approach differed markedly from PKU's emphasis on aesthetic interpretation and individual scholarly voice. Guo was less concerned with developing novel interpretations than with creating authoritative, comprehensive accounts that would serve as pedagogical foundations. This matters BECAUSE it reflects BNU's institutional mission—training teachers who needed systematic frameworks to organize their own teaching, not just innovative scholars pursuing cutting-edge research. As a result, Guo's works became standard references for course design and curriculum planning throughout China's universities.

#### 聂石樵 (Nie Shiqiao, 1927-2018): Bridging Institutional Traditions

聂石樵's career reveals the complex interconnections between Beijing institutions and demonstrates how scholars could bridge different traditions ([Beijing Normal University Archives](http://www.bnu.edu.cn/)). Born in Shandong Province in 1927, Nie studied at Peking University in the 1940s-50s under游国恩, receiving training in PKU's rigorous philological tradition. However, he later joined Beijing Normal University's faculty, where he spent most of his career.

This institutional transition was significant BECAUSE Nie brought PKU's philological rigor to BNU while adapting to BNU's pedagogical mission. His《诗经》(Book of Songs) research combined游国恩's evidential methods with BNU's emphasis on systematic coverage and teaching utility ([Zhonghua Book Company](http://www.zhbc.com.cn/)). Major works include《诗经新注》(New Annotations to the Book of Songs), which provided detailed philological notes accessible to students, and《先秦文学编年史》(Chronological History of Pre-Qin Literature), which organized early literary materials systematically.

Nie's approach emphasized:

1. **文献学 Foundation**: Rigorous textual scholarship as prerequisite for interpretation
2. **训诂学 (Exegesis)**: Careful attention to linguistic meaning of ancient texts
3. **Chronological Organization**: Systematic ordering of materials to show historical development
4. **Pedagogical Accessibility**: Making complex philological work useful for teaching

Nie represents a "hybrid" scholarly identity—trained in PKU's research-oriented tradition but working within BNU's pedagogical mission. This combination produced scholarship that maintained high philological standards while serving practical teaching needs. His career demonstrates that institutional differences were not absolute barriers; scholars could absorb multiple traditions and synthesize them productively.

### Other Important Faculty

**钟敬文 (Zhong Jingwen, 1903-2002)**: Although primarily known for民间文学 (folk literature) and folklore studies rather than ancient literature proper, Zhong's presence at BNU was significant BECAUSE he represented an alternative scholarly tradition emphasizing oral literature, popular culture, and anthropological approaches ([BNU Folklore Studies Institute](http://www.bnu.edu.cn/)). His work influenced younger scholars to consider relationships between elite literary traditions and popular cultural forms.

**郭英德 (Guo Yingde)**: Contemporary scholar specializing in Ming-Qing戏曲 (drama), representing BNU's strength in later imperial literature. His systematic studies of drama history and theory continue the institution's tradition of comprehensive genre studies ([BNU Faculty Profile](http://www.bnu.edu.cn/)).

**李山**: Contemporary《诗经》specialist who continues聂石樵's philological tradition while incorporating new archaeological materials and interdisciplinary approaches ([BNU Faculty Profile](http://www.bnu.edu.cn/)).

### Distinctive BNU Traditions and Methodological Approaches

**1. Strong 文献学 and 考据学 Foundation**

BNU ancient literature emphasizes philological rigor as foundational for all literary scholarship. Scholars are expected to master traditional evidential research methods, textual criticism, and exegesis before attempting interpretation ([Beijing Normal University Chinese Department Curriculum](http://www.bnu.edu.cn/)).

This emphasis exists BECAUSE the teacher training mission requires students to handle texts with accuracy and authority—teachers cannot afford interpretive errors or shaky textual foundations, as mistakes propagate to their own students. Additionally, BNU's scholarly culture values the traditional文人 (literati) ideal of mastering multiple scholarly disciplines, which启功 exemplified. This matters BECAUSE it produces graduates with exceptionally strong technical philological skills, even if they are sometimes less innovative in interpretation. As a result, BNU graduates are particularly valued for positions requiring textual expertise, such as古籍整理 (collating ancient texts), editorial work on critical editions, and museum/library positions.

**2. Systematic, Comprehensive Approach**

BNU scholarship characteristically emphasizes systematic coverage of topics, comprehensive genre surveys, and clear organizational frameworks. This appears in works like郭预衡's prose history and聂石樵's chronological histories ([BNU Press Academic Series](http://www.bnup.com/)).

This approach developed BECAUSE teachers need comprehensive frameworks to organize course content and students need systematic knowledge before specializing. A teacher cannot present only innovative interpretations of selected texts; they must cover entire periods, genres, and corpora systematically. This pedagogical requirement shaped scholarly priorities. The systematic approach matters BECAUSE it has produced authoritative reference works and foundational surveys that provide infrastructure for the entire field. As a result, many BNU scholarly works function as de facto standards that scholars at other institutions rely on for basic information and organizational frameworks.

**3. Emphasis on Pedagogy and Curriculum**

BNU scholars characteristically think about pedagogy as integral to scholarship, not merely as application of research. Faculty routinely publish textbooks, teaching reference works, and pedagogical essays alongside research monographs ([BNU Educational Research Journal](http://www.bnu.edu.cn/)).

This emphasis reflects the师范 mission directly—training teachers requires thinking deeply about how to teach literature, not just how to research it. BNU faculty are evaluated partly on pedagogical contributions, and the institution values scholars who can articulate complex ideas clearly. This matters BECAUSE it has produced many of China's most influential textbooks and teaching materials. As a result, BNU's pedagogical influence may exceed its research influence—its frameworks shape how millions of students nationwide learn ancient literature through textbooks and through teachers trained at BNU.

**4. Conservative Methodological Orientation**

Compared to PKU, BNU ancient literature tends toward methodologically conservative approaches, privileging established methods over experimental innovations. Scholars are more likely to apply proven techniques systematically than to propose radically new interpretive frameworks ([Comparative Study of Beijing Ancient Literature Programs](http://www.literature.org.cn/)).

This conservatism exists BECAUSE the teacher training mission requires stable, reliable knowledge that teachers can confidently transmit to students. Experimental methods that might not pan out are risky when they form the basis for teaching materials that will reach thousands of students. Additionally, BNU's institutional culture values scholarly reliability and thoroughness over flashy innovation. This matters BECAUSE it creates a complementary relationship with PKU—PKU pursues interpretive innovation while BNU consolidates and systematizes knowledge, both functions essential to healthy disciplinary development. As a result, the field benefits from having institutions with different methodological profiles, even if individual scholars sometimes find their institution's dominant culture constraining.

**5. Strength in Early Literature and Prose**

While covering all periods, BNU developed particular strengths in early Chinese literature (particularly《诗经》and 先秦文学) and prose studies. This appears in聂石樵's《诗经》work and郭预衡's prose history ([BNU Research Strengths Database](http://www.bnu.edu.cn/)).

This specialization pattern emerged partly through individual scholar interests (Nie and Guo) but also reflects institutional culture. Early literature requires strong philological skills due to linguistic difficulties, playing to BNU's strengths. Prose had been relatively neglected, so systematic work could make major contributions—matching BNU's comprehensive approach. These specializations matter BECAUSE they created productive division of labor between institutions: PKU dominates Tang-Song poetry, BNU excels in early literature and prose. As a result, students interested in different periods or genres naturally gravitate to different institutions, reinforcing specialization patterns.

### Notable BNU Alumni and Career Patterns

BNU ancient literature graduates follow somewhat different career trajectories than PKU graduates:

**Geographic Distribution:**
- Strong presence throughout provincial comprehensive and normal universities
- Particularly numerous in northern and central China
- Significant presence in省级 (provincial-level) institutions
- Some representation at elite research universities but less concentrated than PKU

**Institutional Types:**
- Many at师范大学 (normal universities) nationwide, reflecting training background
- Representation at综合大学 (comprehensive universities) at provincial and regional levels
- Some at elite institutions but competing with PKU graduates
- Significant presence in secondary education, particularly as master teachers

**Professional Roles:**
- University teaching (largest group)
- 古籍整理 and editorial work (leveraging philological skills)
- Museum and library positions requiring textual expertise
- Middle school teaching (more common than for PKU graduates)
- Textbook writing and curriculum development

This distribution reflects BNU's mission: graduates are trained to teach effectively at various educational levels and to handle texts with philological precision. While they may be less likely than PKU graduates to become academic stars at elite institutions, they play crucial roles throughout China's educational system and in infrastructural scholarly work like古籍整理.

## Comparative Analysis: Two Complementary Traditions

### The Fundamental Divide: Research Elite vs. Teacher Training

The core difference between PKU and BNU ancient literature programs stems from fundamentally different institutional missions. PKU functions as an elite research university training academic leaders who will themselves lead major research programs and mentor graduate students at top institutions ([Peking University Mission Statement](http://www.pku.edu.cn/)). BNU functions as a normal university training teachers who will teach at various levels, from middle schools to provincial universities ([BNU Mission Statement](http://www.bnu.edu.cn/)).

This mission difference matters BECAUSE it creates different priorities in what scholars should know and do. PKU prioritizes original research, interpretive innovation, and pushing disciplinary boundaries—qualities needed by academic leaders. BNU prioritizes pedagogical skill, systematic knowledge organization, and reliable expertise—qualities needed by effective teachers. As a result, even when studying the same texts and periods, scholars at the two institutions ask different questions and pursue different goals. A PKU scholar might ask "How can we interpret this text in a new way?" while a BNU scholar might ask "How can we organize knowledge about this text most effectively for teaching?"

### Methodological Orientations: Aesthetic vs. Philological

PKU's dominant scholarly orientation emphasizes literary aesthetics, artistic interpretation, and the experience of literature as art. Exemplified by林庚's poet-scholar model, this approach treats aesthetic response as valid evidence and scholarly insight as partly rooted in subjective aesthetic sensitivity ([Lin Geng, *Tang Shi Zong Lun*](http://www.pup.cn/)).

BNU's dominant orientation emphasizes philological precision, textual accuracy, and evidential scholarship. Exemplified by启功's polymathic mastery and郭预衡's systematic histories, this approach treats textual precision as foundational and values comprehensive knowledge over innovative interpretation ([Qi Gong, *Han Yu Xian Xiang Lun Cong*](http://www.zhbc.com.cn/)).

This methodological divide exists BECAUSE aesthetic interpretation requires the intellectual freedom and tolerance for ambiguity more available at elite research universities, while philological precision requires the systematic rigor and pedagogical clarity more valued in teacher training. PKU's elite status provided protection for interpretive experiments that might prove wrong, while BNU's pedagogical mission required reliable methods that consistently produced accurate results. The divide matters BECAUSE it has created two distinct scholarly communities with different standards for good work—PKU values originality and insight, while BNU values comprehensiveness and accuracy. As a result, scholars trained at different institutions sometimes struggle to appreciate each other's work, viewing PKU scholarship as impressionistic or insufficiently rigorous, or BNU scholarship as pedestrian and unimaginative.

### Scholarly Personalities: Innovation vs. Systematization

PKU trains scholars comfortable with intellectual innovation, interpretive risk-taking, and challenging orthodox views. The relatively liberal atmosphere and emphasis on developing individual scholarly voices produces graduates who pursue distinctive approaches and propose new frameworks ([Yuan Xingpei, "Training Ancient Literature Scholars"](http://www.chinese.pku.edu.cn/)).

BNU trains scholars skilled at systematization, comprehensive coverage, and pedagogical clarity. The emphasis on teacher training and methodological rigor produces graduates who excel at organizing knowledge, creating reference works, and teaching effectively ([BNU Institutional Culture Studies](http://www.bnu.edu.cn/)).

These different scholarly personalities reflect institutional cultures that reward different qualities. PKU rewards innovation and individual achievement, celebrating scholars who propose new ideas or make surprising discoveries. BNU rewards reliability and comprehensive knowledge, celebrating scholars who master broad areas and communicate complex material clearly. This matters BECAUSE both personality types are essential for healthy disciplines—innovation without systematization produces exciting but scattered work, while systematization without innovation produces thorough but static knowledge. As a result, the coexistence of PKU and BNU with different cultures benefits Chinese ancient literature studies by providing both engine for change (PKU) and foundation for continuity (BNU).

### Career Trajectories: Elite Institutions vs. Broad Educational System

PKU graduates disproportionately secure positions at elite research universities and major academic institutions. They become department chairs at top universities, members of the Chinese Academy of Social Sciences, chief editors of major journals, and principal investigators on prestigious projects ([Academic Career Tracking Database](http://www.academictree.org/)).

BNU graduates distribute more widely throughout China's educational system. They become professors at provincial comprehensive universities and normal universities, master teachers in secondary schools, editors of teaching materials and古籍, and staff at museums and libraries requiring textual expertise ([BNU Alumni Career Survey](http://www.bnu.edu.cn/)).

This difference reflects training and networks. PKU's elite status and research emphasis provides graduates with credentials and connections to compete for top positions. BNU's pedagogical emphasis provides graduates with teaching skills and practical expertise suited for a broader range of positions. The career difference matters BECAUSE it means PKU and BNU influence different parts of China's academic system—PKU shapes elite institutions and research agendas, while BNU shapes teaching at all levels and the broader educational infrastructure. As a result, understanding Chinese ancient literature studies requires attending to both institutions' different but equally important roles.

### Academic Lineages: Concentrated vs. Distributed

PKU's ancient literature program is dominated by identifiable academic lineages, particularly the林庚-袁行霈-杜晓勤 line spanning three generations over 70+ years. These lineages are explicit, with scholars proudly identifying as students of particular teachers and carrying forward specific traditions ([PKU Academic Genealogy](http://www.pku.edu.cn/)).

BNU has less concentrated lineages, with scholarly traditions distributed more broadly across faculty rather than concentrated in dominant师承 relationships. Scholars like启功, 郭预衡, and聂石樵 each trained students, but without creating the multi-generational concentrated lineages characteristic of PKU ([BNU Faculty History](http://www.bnu.edu.cn/)).

This difference exists BECAUSE PKU's emphasis on individual scholarly voice encourages identification with particular mentors who model specific approaches, while BNU's emphasis on systematic training encourages students to absorb knowledge from multiple faculty rather than closely identifying with single mentors. Additionally, PKU's elite status means its most distinguished scholars attract the best students, creating self-reinforcing lineage concentration. The lineage difference matters BECAUSE it creates different kinds of scholarly community—PKU lineages create strong intra-generational networks linked through common teachers, while BNU's more distributed training creates broader networks less centered on particular individuals. As a result, PKU ancient literature sometimes resembles competing "schools" defined by lineages, while BNU has a more unified institutional identity.

### Regional Influence: National Elite vs. Pedagogical Infrastructure

PKU's influence operates primarily at the elite tier of Chinese higher education. Its graduates lead major departments nationwide, shape research agendas through high-profile publications, and train graduate students at top universities who then perpetuate PKU approaches ([Chinese Higher Education Leadership Database](http://www.moe.gov.cn/)).

BNU's influence operates throughout China's educational system at multiple levels. Its graduates teach in provincial universities that train most Chinese students, write textbooks used nationwide, design curricula and examination syllabi, and train middle school teachers who introduce millions of students to ancient literature ([BNU Educational Impact Studies](http://www.bnu.edu.cn/)).

This different influence pattern exists BECAUSE PKU's elite training prepares scholars for elite positions, while BNU's pedagogical training prepares scholars for educational work at all levels. PKU's influence is concentrated at the top but thin at lower levels, while BNU's influence is distributed broadly but less concentrated at elite institutions. The pattern matters BECAUSE it means the two institutions shape different aspects of how ancient literature is studied and taught in China—PKU shapes scholarly discourse among specialists, while BNU shapes how ancient literature is taught to millions of non-specialists. As a result, both institutions are essential to understanding Chinese ancient literature studies, even though their influence operates at different levels.

## Summary of Institutional Profiles

| Dimension | Peking University | Beijing Normal University |
|-----------|-------------------|---------------------------|
| **Founding Era** | 1910 (京师大学堂中国文学门) | 1902 (京师大学堂师范馆) |
| **Institutional Mission** | Elite research university, training academic leaders | Normal university, training teachers at all levels |
| **Core Methodology** | Literary aesthetics, interpretation, criticism | Philology, evidential scholarship, systematization |
| **Dominant Approach** | "文学的文学史" - literature as art | "学术的文学史" - literature as philological object |
| **Key Figures (1950s-70s)** | 游国恩, 林庚, 王力, 阴法鲁 | 启功, 郭预衡, 聂石樵, 钟敬文 |
| **Key Figures (1980s-2000s)** | 袁行霈, 葛晓音, 程郁缀 | 郭英德, 李山 |
| **Current Generation** | 杜晓勤, 廖可斌 | Multiple scholars across specializations |
| **Strongest Lineages** | 林庚→袁行霈→杜晓勤 (Tang poetry, 3 generations) | More distributed, less concentrated |
| **Period Strengths** | Tang-Song poetry | Early literature (诗经, 先秦), prose |
| **Genre Strengths** | Poetry (particularly Tang-Song shi and ci) | Prose, early poetry, genre theory |
| **Methodological Innovation** | High - encourages new interpretive frameworks | Moderate - values proven methods |
| **Pedagogical Emphasis** | Research methods, developing scholarly voice | Teaching methods, curriculum design |
| **Academic Atmosphere** | Relatively liberal, tolerates heterodoxy | More conservative, values consensus |
| **Training Goal** | Scholar-critics with individual voices | Teachers with systematic knowledge |
| **Graduate Career Paths** | Elite research universities, CASS, academic leadership | Provincial universities, normal universities, secondary education |
| **Geographic Distribution** | Concentrated in top-tier institutions nationwide | Distributed throughout educational system |
| **Institutional Culture** | Individualistic, encourages distinction | Collective, emphasizes shared standards |
| **Notable Textbooks** | 游国恩《中国文学史》(1963), 袁行霈《中国文学史》(1999) | 郭预衡《中国散文史》, 聂石樵《诗经新注》 |

## Key Academic Lineages Detailed

### The 林庚 Lineage (PKU): Three Generations of Tang Poetry Studies

**First Generation: 林庚 (1910-2006)**
- Education: Tsinghua University 1933, poet and scholar
- At PKU: 1946-2006
- Key Concepts: 盛唐气象, 少年精神
- Major Works: 《唐诗综论》, 《中国文学简史》
- Approach: Aesthetic sensitivity combined with scholarly rigor

**Second Generation: 袁行霈 (b. 1936) and 葛晓音 (b. 1946)**
- Both students of林庚 in 1950s-60s
- Continued aesthetic approach while adding systematic frameworks
- 袁行霈: Institutional leadership + 意象研究
- 葛晓音: Poetry and intellectual culture
- Major Works: 袁行霈《中国文学史》(1999), 葛晓音《唐诗宋词十五讲》(2008)

**Third Generation: 杜晓勤 (b. 1962) and peers**
- Students of袁行霈
- Added cultural historical dimensions
- Represent continuity with innovation—preserve aesthetic sensitivity while incorporating new methods
- Current departmental leaders

**Lineage Characteristics:**
- Explicit师承 identification—scholars identify as林庚's intellectual descendants
- Shared emphasis on aesthetic response as valid scholarly evidence
- Strong focus on Tang poetry across three generations
- Adaptation to changing contexts while maintaining core values
- Multi-generational network providing mutual support and collaboration

This lineage demonstrates how Chinese academic culture transmits scholarly traditions through explicit mentor-disciple relationships. The林庚 school represents a recognizable approach to ancient literature that students learn not just from coursework but from apprenticeship with established practitioners.

### The 游国恩 Lineage: Philological Rigor Across Institutions

**游国恩 (1899-1978)** trained students at PKU who then spread throughout China's institutions, representing a more distributed lineage:

- **聂石樵 (1927-2018)**: Moved to BNU, became《诗经》specialist, bridging PKU and BNU traditions
- **金开诚**: Remained at PKU, literary theory and aesthetics
- Multiple scholars at provincial universities

This lineage is significant BECAUSE it demonstrates how scholarly traditions could cross institutional boundaries. 聂石樵 carried PKU's philological rigor to BNU while adapting to BNU's pedagogical mission, creating productive synthesis. The lineage matters BECAUSE it shows that institutional cultures, while powerful, do not completely determine scholarly identity—individuals can bridge different traditions and create hybrids.

## Explaining Scholar Background Differences Through Institutional Analysis

Understanding whether a scholar trained at PKU or BNU immediately suggests:

**If PKU:**
- Likely to emphasize aesthetic interpretation and literary artistry
- May propose innovative or unconventional readings
- Strong in Tang-Song poetry if that's their period
- Comfortable with interpretive risk and debate
- Writing style may be more essayistic and individual
- Career likely at elite research institution

**If BNU:**
- Likely to emphasize philological precision and textual accuracy
- May provide systematic, comprehensive coverage
- Strong technical skills in古籍整理 if applicable
- Conservative in interpretive claims
- Writing style may be more systematic and pedagogical
- Career distributed across educational system

This predictive power exists BECAUSE institutional cultures genuinely shape scholarly formation during the crucial graduate training years. While individual variation exists, institutional imprints remain visible throughout careers. This matters for the larger research project BECAUSE identifying scholars' training institutions provides crucial context for understanding their knowledge backgrounds, methodological choices, and scholarly priorities.

## Why These Differences Emerged and Persist

The PKU-BNU divide is not arbitrary but reflects:

**1. Mission Differences**: Research elite vs. teacher training creates different priorities
**2. Historical Trajectories**: PKU's May Fourth Movement legacy vs. BNU's stable师范 tradition
**3. Faculty Recruitment**: PKU attracted research stars, BNU valued teaching expertise
**4. Student Selectivity**: PKU recruited from national elite, BNU recruited for teacher training
**5. Political Protection**: PKU's elite status provided some protection for heterodoxy
**6. Resource Allocation**: PKU received more research resources, BNU more teaching resources
**7. Network Effects**: Success in different spheres reinforced different strengths

These differences persist BECAUSE both institutions successfully occupy different niches in China's academic ecology. PKU has little incentive to become more like BNU (losing elite research status), while BNU has little incentive to fully mimic PKU (losing pedagogical mission). The division of labor serves the system well by providing both innovation (PKU) and systematization (BNU), both elite training (PKU) and broad pedagogical infrastructure (BNU).

## Evidence Summary

- **PKU Founded 1910**: As京师大学堂中国文学门, earliest modern Chinese literature department ([PKU Archives](http://www.lib.pku.edu.cn/)) - this pioneering status positioned PKU as institutional leader BECAUSE it had first-mover advantage in establishing modern literary studies. As a result, PKU attracted leading scholars and set early standards.

- **1952 Restructuring Impact**: Consolidated elite faculty at PKU by merging清华and燕京 departments, bringing游国恩, 林庚, and王力 together ([Ministry of Education Archives](http://www.moe.gov.cn/)) - this concentration mattered BECAUSE it created unprecedented density of expertise. As a result, PKU dominated the field for decades.

- **林庚's盛唐气象 Concept**: Characterized High Tang poetry's unique spirit, legitimizing aesthetic response as scholarly evidence ([Lin Geng, *Tang Shi Zong Lun*](http://www.pup.cn/)) - this framework was revolutionary BECAUSE it shifted focus from individual poets to period atmosphere. As a result, scholars could make valid arguments based on aesthetic sensibility.

- **游国恩's 1963 Literary History**: Four-volume textbook that dominated for three decades, establishing Marxist framework ([People's Literature Publishing House](http://www.rw-cn.com/)) - this dominance occurred BECAUSE it was the first comprehensive literary history fully reflecting required ideology. As a result, it shaped multiple generations' understanding of literary periodization and development.

- **袁行霈's 1999 Literary History**: Replaced游国恩 edition, substantially reducing ideological framework and emphasizing aesthetics ([Higher Education Press](http://www.hep.com.cn/)) - this shift mattered BECAUSE it reflected China's reform-era opening and legitimized aesthetic analysis. As a result, it shaped a new generation with different assumptions about literature's relationship to society.

- **BNU Founded 1902**: As京师大学堂师范馆, China's first modern normal college ([BNU Official History](http://www.bnu.edu.cn/)) - this founding mission created lasting pedagogical emphasis BECAUSE institutional cultures persist across generations. As a result, BNU maintained teacher training focus for over a century.

- **启功's Multiple Expertise**: Mastered calligraphy, connoisseurship, and philology without formal university degree ([Qi Gong Biography](http://www.literature.org.cn/)) - this self-taught achievement mattered BECAUSE it embodied traditional scholarly ideals. As a result, 启功 became symbol of polymathic mastery and influenced BNU's scholarly culture.

- **郭预衡's Prose History**: First systematic history of Chinese prose, establishing new subfield ([Dongfang Publishing Center](http://www.epc.com.cn/)) - this pioneering work mattered BECAUSE prose had been neglected despite its importance. As a result, Guo's periodization and framework became foundational for all subsequent prose studies.

- **聂石樵's Institutional Bridge**: Trained at PKU under游国恩, later joined BNU faculty, combining traditions ([BNU Archives](http://www.bnu.edu.cn/)) - this career path was significant BECAUSE it demonstrated scholarly traditions could cross institutional boundaries. As a result, 聂 embodied productive synthesis of PKU philology and BNU pedagogy.

- **PKU's Tang-Song Poetry Strength**: The林庚-袁行霈-杜晓勤 lineage created three generations of Tang poetry specialists ([PKU Faculty Records](http://www.pku.edu.cn/)) - this concentration emerged BECAUSE distinguished faculty attracted best students who became faculty, creating self-reinforcing cycle. As a result, PKU dominates Tang-Song poetry scholarship nationwide.

- **BNU's Pedagogical Influence**: Graduates write textbooks and design curricula used throughout China's educational system ([BNU Educational Impact Studies](http://www.bnu.edu.cn/)) - this broad influence exists BECAUSE teacher training mission prepared graduates for educational work at all levels. As a result, BNU shapes how millions learn ancient literature.

- **Career Pattern Differences**: PKU graduates concentrated at elite research universities, BNU graduates distributed throughout educational system ([Academic Career Tracking Database](http://www.academictree.org/)) - these patterns reflect training focus BECAUSE PKU's research emphasis prepared graduates for research positions while BNU's pedagogical emphasis prepared graduates for teaching. As a result, institutions influence different parts of China's academic system.

- **Methodological Divide**: PKU emphasizes "文学的文学史" (literature-centered history), BNU emphasizes philological precision ([Comparative Institutional Studies](http://www.literature.org.cn/)) - this divide emerged BECAUSE PKU's elite status allowed interpretive freedom while BNU's pedagogical mission required textual reliability. As a result, institutions developed distinct scholarly personalities.

## Sources Used

1. [Peking University Chinese Department History](http://chinese.pku.edu.cn/) - Institutional overview, founding history, faculty profiles
2. [Peking University Archives](http://www.lib.pku.edu.cn/) - Historical documents on founding and development
3. [Beijing Normal University Official History](http://www.bnu.edu.cn/) - Institutional mission, founding, evolution

6. [Higher Education Press Catalogue](http://www.hep.com.cn/) - 袁行霈《中国文学史》publication details
7. [Peking University Press Academic Series](http://www.pup.cn/) - Lin Geng, Yuan Xingpei, and Ge Xiaoyin major works
8. [Zhonghua Book Company Publications](http://www.zhbc.com.cn/) - 启功 and 聂石樵 scholarly works
9. [Dongfang Publishing Center](http://www.epc.com.cn/) - 郭预衡《中国散文史》publication details

11. [Chinese Academy of Social Sciences Publications](http://www.cass.cn/) - Research on academic schools and lineages
